# Implementation Log

## 2026-03-10 - Add The First Image-Side Text Renderer Slice
- Added the first real Phase 3 renderer slice by extending the selector surface in [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz) and the selector ceilings in [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c), and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). The important point is architectural, not just mechanical: the image can now host its own text-rendering behavior on top of `BitBlt`, `Glyphs`, `Font`, `TextMetrics`, and `TextLayout`, instead of relying exclusively on the ad hoc C-side text loop.
- Added the focused proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_image_side_text_renderer_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_image_side_text_renderer_demo.rz). That example creates a dynamic `TextRenderer` class from source inside the running image, installs live-source methods onto it, and renders styled text onto `Display defaultForm`. This keeps the implementation aligned with the docs and the current bootstrap stage: the low-level VM still only provides bitmap primitives and object/message execution, while text drawing policy starts moving upward into normal Recorz source.
- Kept the first slice deliberately small and honest to the current runtime limits. The renderer uses one readable public entry point, `drawStyledText:onForm:`, and a compact internal live-source recursion path to walk characters with the newly added `String>>size` / `String>>at:` support. I did not widen the compiled-method format or invent a second rendering subsystem just to make this land.
- Raised only the RV32 `dev` heap budget in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.h) from `768` to `1024` objects. That is a development-capacity change, not a target-profile change: the renderer proof exercises the same live-source/context path the eventual image-side tools will use, and the previous `dev` heap was too tight even for this first nontrivial renderer slice. The `target` profile remains unchanged.
- Added the screenshot proof in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_render_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_render_integration.py). The RV32 render suite now boots the image-side renderer demo, verifies the serial marker `IMAGE RENDERER`, and checks that the framebuffer region at the text origin contains the expected foreground/background pixel mix.
- Marked the first Phase 3 checkbox complete in [TODO.md](/Users/david/repos/recorz/TODO.md): Recorz now has a real Smalltalk-shaped text renderer drawing onto `Form`/`Bitmap` through existing primitives, even though the workspace/browser C fallback remains in place for the next steps.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_render_integration.QemuRiscv32RenderIntegrationTests.test_image_side_text_renderer_draws_pixels_via_live_source -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Add Minimal Image-Side String Traversal For Text Work
- Added the smallest missing string surface needed for image-owned text work: `String>>size` and `String>>at:` on both [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). The runtime still keeps strings as immediate VM values, but the image can now measure and traverse them directly instead of depending on C-only text walkers.
- Extended the kernel selector set in [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz) and synced the selector ceilings in [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c). This keeps the RV32-first program/image contract honest before the first image-side renderer methods start sending `size` during normal boot and interactive work.
- Added the focused proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_string_size_at_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_string_size_at_demo.rz) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The running image now prints `SIZE=3` and `AT=66` for `'ABC'`, which is enough to support the upcoming glyph-by-glyph image-side renderer without introducing collections or a broader string API prematurely.
- Updated the lowering expectations in [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py) so the generated selector registry includes `#size`.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_strings_support_size_and_at_from_the_image -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Add Image-Side Cursor And Selection Model Objects
- Added real image-visible cursor/selection classes in [kernel/mvp/TextCursor.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextCursor.rz) and [kernel/mvp/TextSelection.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextSelection.rz), then seeded `WorkspaceCursor` and `WorkspaceSelection` as singleton boot objects in the after-glyph family. This closes the next unchecked Phase 2 item in [TODO.md](/Users/david/repos/recorz/TODO.md) without trying to move rendering into the image prematurely.
- Exposed those objects through normal image code in [kernel/mvp/Workspace.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Workspace.rz). `Workspace>>cursor` and `Workspace>>selection` are just normal compiled methods returning seeded globals, and the accessors on `TextCursor` / `TextSelection` make line, column, top-line, and collapsed-selection endpoints inspectable from Recorz code instead of being trapped in the VM’s serialized input-monitor state string.
- Kept the VM role narrow on both [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c): whenever the existing interactive workspace updates its cursor state, the runtime now mirrors that state into the seeded cursor/selection objects. The editor still owns movement and persistence for now, but the cursor model is no longer hidden implementation detail.
- Synced the seed/runtime contract around the new model in [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz), [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), [platform/qemu-riscv32/seed.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/seed.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/seed.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/seed.c), [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.h), [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.h), [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py), and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py). That raised the class/object/selector/global ceilings cleanly while preserving the RV32-first seed/image format.
- Added the focused live proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_cursor_selection_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_cursor_selection_demo.rz) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The running image now enters the interactive workspace, performs a small cursor edit, exits, and prints `Workspace cursor` / `Workspace selection` fields over serial, proving those text-state objects are usable from inside Recorz.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_cursor_and_selection_objects_are_visible_from_the_image -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Add Image-Side Text Layout Objects For Margins, Wrapping, And Tabs
- Added a real image-visible layout model in [kernel/mvp/TextLayout.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextLayout.rz), [kernel/mvp/TextMargins.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextMargins.rz), and [kernel/mvp/TextFlow.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextFlow.rz). `TranscriptLayout` is now a nested object graph with margins, pixel scale, line spacing, and flow policy rather than a VM-only tuple of hard-coded constants, which closes the next unchecked Phase 2 step in [TODO.md](/Users/david/repos/recorz/TODO.md) without widening the MVP heap object shape.
- Extended the image-side surface in [kernel/mvp/Display.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Display.rz) and [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz) so Recorz code can inspect layout policy directly through `Display layout`, `margins`, `flow`, `left`, `top`, `right`, `bottom`, `scale`, `lineSpacing`, `wrapWidth`, `tabWidth`, and `lineBreakMode`. The focused proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_display_layout_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_display_layout_demo.rz) exercises those accessors from inside the running image.
- Kept the C runtime limited to primitive rendering and input, while moving layout decisions upward. Both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) now resolve text margins, wrap width, tab width, and line-break mode through the seeded layout objects. Workspace/editor sizing, transcript line advance, wrapping, and tab expansion all consult that image-owned structure instead of ad hoc constants.
- Synced the bootstrap/runtime contract in [tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py), [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py), and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py) to the richer model. The fixed boot-object family now seeds `TranscriptMargins` and `TranscriptFlow` before `TranscriptLayout`, selector ceilings moved to `RECORZ_MVP_SELECTOR_LINE_BREAK_MODE`, and the inspector/lowering expectations now match the new object graph and root indices.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_layout_objects_are_visible_from_the_image tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_point_size_is_visible_from_the_image tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_metrics_are_visible_from_the_image tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_can_render_styled_text_from_image_objects -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Represent Text Style Separately From Raw Strings
- Added a real image-side `StyledText` object in [kernel/mvp/StyledText.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/StyledText.rz) and promoted [kernel/mvp/TextStyle.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextStyle.rz) into the source-boot set with `foregroundColor`, `backgroundColor`, and `withText:`. That closes the next unchecked Phase 2 item in [TODO.md](/Users/david/repos/recorz/TODO.md) without widening the MVP heap shape beyond one small new object kind.
- Extended the Smalltalk-shaped text surface in [kernel/mvp/Form.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Form.rz) and [kernel/mvp/Display.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Display.rz) with `writeStyledText:` and `Display>>style`. The builder in [tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py) now lowers `Display style` through the seeded transcript-style root, so image code can construct and inspect styled text directly instead of treating colors as hidden VM-only policy.
- Kept the VM role limited to primitive drawing while moving style ownership upward. Both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) now understand `TextStyle>>withText:` and `Form>>writeStyledText:` as narrow primitives that read the styled object’s `text` and `style` fields, then render with image-provided foreground/background colors. Raw-string rendering still exists for compatibility, but the style choice is now image-visible and inspectable.
- Synced the shared runtime contract to the richer text model by adding the new selectors, object kind, primitive bindings, and generated limits across [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz), [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py). The lowering and header tests were also tightened to use dynamic primitive ids where appropriate so legitimate text-model growth stops breaking brittle constant tails.
- Added the focused RV32 proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_display_styled_text_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_display_styled_text_demo.rz) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The running image now constructs `styled := Display style withText: 'STYLE'`, renders it, and can inspect both `styled text` and `styled style foregroundColor` from Recorz code, proving text style is no longer fused into raw string handling.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_point_size_is_visible_from_the_image tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_metrics_are_visible_from_the_image tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_can_render_styled_text_from_image_objects -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Represent Transcript Glyph Metrics And Vertical Metrics In Image Objects
- Extended the image-side text model with a real nested vertical-metrics object instead of widening the MVP heap format. [kernel/mvp/TextMetrics.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextMetrics.rz) now carries `cellWidth`, `cellHeight`, `baseline`, and `verticalMetrics`, and the new [kernel/mvp/TextVerticalMetrics.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/TextVerticalMetrics.rz) carries `ascent`, `descent`, and `lineHeight`. This keeps the object memory shape stable while still moving the important typography geometry into inspectable Recorz objects, which is exactly the second unchecked Phase 2 item in [TODO.md](/Users/david/repos/recorz/TODO.md).
- Promoted `TextMetrics` and `TextVerticalMetrics` into the kernel source-boot order so their accessors become real built-in methods available inside the running image, not dead declarations. That required extending the source-boot class sequence in the kernel files and syncing the shared contract tests in [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py) to the new class, selector, boot-object, and compiled-method counts.
- Added new image-visible selectors in [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz) for `cellWidth`, `cellHeight`, `baseline`, `verticalMetrics`, `ascent`, `descent`, and `lineHeight`, along with accessor methods on the metrics classes. The focused proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_display_font_metrics_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_display_font_metrics_demo.rz) now prints those values directly from Recorz code via `Display font metrics ...`, proving the geometry lives in the image model rather than only in C constants.
- Updated both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) to resolve transcript row advance through the new image-owned `lineHeight`, validate `baseline` / `ascent` / `descent` / `lineHeight` consistency at boot and snapshot reload, and keep primitive drawing limited to pixel work. The VM still owns bitmap blits and cursor painting, but the line-geometry policy is now pulled from image objects instead of ad hoc constants.
- Synced the bootstrap/runtime substrate to the expanded text model without broadening its role: selector ceilings moved to `RECORZ_MVP_SELECTOR_LINE_HEIGHT` in [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), max object-kind bounds now include `TextVerticalMetrics` in both runtimes, and [tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py) now exposes the small-integer subset of mixed boot objects so `TranscriptMetrics` can own both scalar and object fields cleanly.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_point_size_is_visible_from_the_image tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_metrics_are_visible_from_the_image -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Add An Image-Visible Font Object For Transcript Rendering
- Added a real `Font` kernel class in [kernel/mvp/Font.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Font.rz) with image-visible `glyphs`, `metrics`, `behavior`, and `pointSize` fields, then seeded `TranscriptFont` as a new kernel root. This is the first deliberate move of text-rendering policy out of “anonymous VM state” and into inspectable image objects, which is exactly the first Phase 2 step in [TODO.md](/Users/david/repos/recorz/TODO.md).
- Kept the Smalltalk shape clean instead of growing the primitive surface unnecessarily. `Display>>font` in [kernel/mvp/Display.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Display.rz) is a normal compiled method that lowers to the new `transcript_font` root in [tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py), mirroring the existing `Display>>defaultForm` path. That keeps the image-side object model richer without paying for a new ad hoc VM-only primitive API.
- Updated both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) so transcript rendering now resolves metrics, behavior, and glyph ownership through `TranscriptFont`. The low-level bitmap writes are still VM-side, but the runtime now validates that the live font object points at the expected glyph table and supporting text objects instead of assuming hidden fixed roots.
- Synced the manual C-side bounds that still matter to the bootstrap/runtime substrate: selector ceilings in [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), selector/root ceilings in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c), root-array sizing in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.h) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.h), and root binding validation in [platform/qemu-riscv32/seed.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/seed.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/seed.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/seed.c). That keeps RV32 as the primary live target while maintaining RV64 as a consistent validation build.
- Extended the builder/inspection contract in [tools/inspect_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/inspect_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py), [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py), and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector.py) so the new class, root, selector set, and compiled-method counts are treated as first-class kernel structure rather than an incidental change.
- Added the focused RV32 proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_display_font_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_display_font_demo.rz) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py): the running image can now answer `Display font pointSize` and print `16` over serial, proving the font object is visible and usable from Recorz code, not just from the C runtime.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_display_font_point_size_is_visible_from_the_image -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Prove The RV32 In-Image Development Loop End To End
- Added a focused end-to-end RV32 regression in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py) that drives the actual framebuffer/editor workflow instead of a narrower component path. The test now boots the package editor from [qemu_riscv_workspace_edit_current_package_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_edit_current_package_demo.rz), accepts the current package source from inside the image, runs package tests in the same editor session, emits a live snapshot, and then cold-reloads from that snapshot.
- The proof checks the loop at three layers: the save log confirms `accept`, `test`, and snapshot shutdown all happened in the interactive session; the snapshot inspector confirms the saved image is still in the input monitor with the `Tests` package editor target and `TEST OK` status; and the reload run confirms the framebuffer comes back in the same in-image development surface without host-side demo-specific startup behavior.
- This is the milestone-closing proof for the current lane: the RV32 image can now support a credible development cycle of browse/edit, accept, test, save, reboot, and continue. The host side is still needed for packaging and booting, but the working state and the development actions themselves are now demonstrably image-owned.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.QemuRiscv32SnapshotIntegrationTests.test_snapshot_proves_the_interactive_package_development_loop -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_save_a_recovery_snapshot tests.test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.QemuRiscv32SnapshotIntegrationTests.test_snapshot_can_reopen_workspace_input_monitor_state_without_demo_specific_program tests.test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.QemuRiscv32SnapshotIntegrationTests.test_snapshot_preserves_input_monitor_status_and_feedback_tail -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Add An Editor-Side Recovery Snapshot Path
- Added a real recovery action to the interactive framebuffer editor on both [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). `Ctrl-K` in the input monitor now routes to the existing `Workspace saveRecoverySnapshot` semantics, so a risky in-image edit can emit a clean rollback snapshot directly from the editor instead of forcing a host-side manual save flow.
- Kept the implementation aligned with the image-owned model rather than inventing a second recovery format. The new editor path simply calls a shared `workspace_save_recovery_snapshot_in_place` helper, which clears the volatile browser target, configures `Workspace reopen` as the startup hook, emits the live snapshot, and shuts the machine down. That makes the editor recovery behavior consistent with the recovery snapshot primitive already present in the kernel.
- Preserved another useful piece of groundwork in the same pass: browser-backed accepts now remember the currently installed class/package/method source before installing the edited replacement. That keeps a last-known-good source reference available inside the image for later recovery-oriented tools, while staying Smalltalk-shaped and inspectable instead of adding a hidden editor diff store.

## 2026-03-10 - Preserve Interactive Editor Status And Feedback Across Snapshots
- Extended the interactive input-monitor state encoding on both [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) so snapshots now preserve not just cursor, viewport, and browser context, but also the current status text and the visible feedback tail. The runtime still stores this state in the image-visible `Workspace` browser target string, which keeps the design small and inspectable instead of introducing a second hidden editor-state object graph.
- Added percent-encoded `STATUS` and `FEEDBACK` segments to the input-monitor state format and taught the runtime to restore them whenever the editor is reopened from a saved snapshot. That means a saved `print it`, test run, or accept/revert/test status now comes back as part of the live workspace session instead of being lost at snapshot time.
- Extended the host-side snapshot inspector in [tools/inspect_qemu_riscv_snapshot.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/inspect_qemu_riscv_snapshot.py) so it can decode the richer input-monitor state directly. The inspector now reports a structured `input_monitor_state` summary with cursor, top line, saved browser target, status, and feedback, which makes snapshot-state proofs much easier to reason about from the outside.
- Tightened the RV32 snapshot harness in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py) so interactive save tests now wait for the framebuffer editor to reach `VIEW: INPUT` before sending keystrokes. That matches the real editor workflow and avoids racing the boot banner when snapshot-driven editor tests exercise `Ctrl-P` and `Ctrl-W` back-to-back.
- Added focused coverage in [tests/test_qemu_riscv_snapshot_inspector.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_snapshot_inspector.py) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py) to prove both sides of the feature: the saved snapshot now contains structured editor state, and reloading that snapshot on RV32 redraws the interactive workspace with the preserved status/feedback surface intact.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_snapshot_inspector tests.test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.QemuRiscv32SnapshotIntegrationTests.test_snapshot_can_reopen_workspace_input_monitor_state_without_demo_specific_program tests.test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.QemuRiscv32SnapshotIntegrationTests.test_snapshot_preserves_input_monitor_status_and_feedback_tail -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-10 - Add Safer Snapshot Backup And Restore Commands For The Interactive Dev Loop
- Tightened the host-side save/resume workflow in [platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile). Both `continue-snapshot` and `continue-snapshot-interactive` now preserve the previous snapshot as `$(SNAPSHOT_PAYLOAD).bak` before replacing it with the newly emitted image state, so an in-image save no longer destroys the last known-good session state.
- Added explicit `dev-reset` and `dev-restore` targets on both QEMU platforms. `dev-reset` recreates the development snapshot from the normal save example, and `dev-restore` rolls the dev loop back to the last preserved backup snapshot. That keeps the current RV32-first interactive workflow small and pragmatic while making the save/resume path feel more like a normal image-development action than a one-way snapshot overwrite.
- Kept the design aligned with the existing architecture: the image still owns the live session and emits snapshots, while the host side is reduced to packaging, file rotation, and restart control. This is the right split for the current self-hosting stage because it improves recovery without moving VM semantics back into Python.
- Extended the Makefile coverage in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_makefile.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_makefile.py) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_makefile.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_makefile.py) so both RV32 and RV64 now prove backup creation in the continue paths and the new `dev-reset` / `dev-restore` command shapes.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_makefile tests.test_qemu_riscv_makefile -v`.

## 2026-03-09 - Make Interactive Save And Resume A First-Class Dev Loop
- Closed the remaining host-workflow gap after `Ctrl-W` by teaching the platform Makefiles how to treat an interactive save as an update to the live snapshot file instead of a serial stream the user has to harvest manually. Both [platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile) now have `continue-snapshot-interactive`, which runs QEMU with a logged stdio chardev and overwrites the input snapshot only if the session actually emits a new `recorz-snapshot-*` payload.
- Added `dev-interactive` on both platform targets as the first real “resume my saved image and keep working” wrapper. It auto-initializes `DEV_SNAPSHOT` if needed through the existing `dev-init` flow, then boots the saved snapshot back into the interactive path. This keeps the save/resume behavior aligned with the image-owned model while making the host-side entry point much closer to a normal Smalltalk image loop.
- Kept the implementation deliberately host-thin. There is no new persistence format and no extra builder-side snapshot logic; the image still owns saving, and the host side now just captures the already-emitted snapshot from an interactive session and places it back at the stable snapshot path.
- Strengthened the host-side proofs in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_makefile.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_makefile.py) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv_makefile.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_makefile.py) with dry-run assertions for `continue-snapshot-interactive` and `dev-interactive`, while keeping the live RV32 runtime proof in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py) focused on the underlying input-monitor save/reopen round-trip that the new Makefile workflow wraps.
- This is the next clean step toward a usable in-image development loop. Saving from the framebuffer editor now has a direct host path back to the stable snapshot file, so the next remaining polish is around command/help ergonomics and the higher-level browser/test workflow rather than raw snapshot plumbing.

## 2026-03-09 - Make Snapshot Save End Cleanly Instead Of Hanging
- Polished the save/reopen path by turning snapshot emission into an explicit terminal action on both runtimes. After writing the `recorz-snapshot-*` stream in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c), the VM now logs `snapshot saved, shutting down` and requests a real machine shutdown instead of returning to `main` and falling into `machine_wait_forever()`.
- Added a tiny machine-level shutdown primitive in [platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c), and the matching headers. The implementation uses the SBI system-reset extension with the shutdown reset type, which keeps the behavior appropriate for both QEMU now and future RISC-V targets that honor SBI shutdown.
- This keeps the architecture cleaner than trying to special-case `Ctrl-W` in the editor loop. Any image-owned save path that emits a live snapshot now has one clear meaning: save the image state and stop the current machine session. That matches how the host-side `save-snapshot` / `continue-snapshot` flows already treat snapshot emission.
- Strengthened the RV32 proofs in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py) and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py). The interactive save test now waits for QEMU to exit cleanly after `Ctrl-W` and proves the shutdown marker is present, and the snapshot round-trip proof for the interactive input monitor now checks for the same end-of-save marker in the captured log.
- This is a focused save/reopen polish step, not a new persistence model. The next clean work is to reduce the remaining mismatch between “save snapshot and stop” versus “resume naturally,” so the normal in-image loop can feel more like an image action and less like a host extraction procedure.

## 2026-03-09 - Polish The Interactive Workspace Command Model
- Reworked the interactive editor command surface on both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) so the primary commands are closer to a real Smalltalk workspace. `Ctrl-D` is now the primary `do it` binding, `Ctrl-P` remains `print it`, `Ctrl-O` is the close/return action, and `Ctrl-R` remains as a compatibility alias for the earlier MVP `run` command.
- Kept the change small and inspectable by reusing the existing editor/browser machinery instead of adding a second command layer. Closing the editor now always goes through the same `Ctrl-O` path: in a browser-backed session it returns to the remembered method or package browser, and in a plain workspace session it simply exits the input monitor cleanly.
- Tightened the feedback text to match the new semantics. The status pane now reports `DOIT USE CTRL-X`, `DOING`, and `DOIT OK` on the do-it path instead of the older run-oriented labels, which makes the framebuffer tool surface less transport-oriented and more image-tool oriented.
- Updated [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py) so the live RV32 proofs exercise the new primary bindings. The interactive editor tests now use `Ctrl-D` for do-it, `Ctrl-P` for print-it, and `Ctrl-O` for close/return, while still proving that method/package editors safely redirect do-it toward `acceptCurrent`.
- This completes a useful command-model polish step without locking in a heavy UI architecture. The next clean work is either feedback/revert polish inside the editor, or save/resume polish so the in-image loop feels less like a snapshot export and more like a normal image action.

## 2026-03-09 - Add Smalltalk-Shaped Print It To The Interactive Workspace
- Added a real `print it` path to the interactive editor on both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). The input-monitor evaluator now returns a real value instead of discarding it, and `Ctrl-P` prints that resulting value into the existing `OUT>` feedback pane while preserving the live editor buffer and browser context.
- Fixed the underlying workspace do-it semantics at the same time: the live workspace compiler now keeps the final statement value instead of unconditionally popping every statement and returning `nil`. That makes `print it` honest and also moves the do-it path closer to normal Smalltalk behavior.
- Moved the editor bindings one step closer to classic Smalltalk expectations by reclaiming `Ctrl-P` for `print it`. Arrow-up still handles upward line motion, and the on-screen legend now advertises `PRINT: CTRL-P` instead of treating `Ctrl-P` as a second cursor-up key.
- Kept the implementation inspectable and aligned with the current MVP architecture. Numbers and strings still use the VM's existing `printString` send semantics, while `nil`, named singleton objects, and other heap objects fall back to the same image-facing value naming path the browser already uses. That avoids inventing a hidden formatter subsystem just to support the interactive editor.
- Strengthened [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py) with focused RV32 proofs for `Ctrl-P` in the plain workspace editor and for the browser-backed safety case. The new tests prove that `1 + 2` prints `OUT> 3`, that method editors report `PRINT USE CTRL-X` instead of trying to run method source as a do-it, and that vertical cursor motion still works via arrow-up plus `Ctrl-N`.
- This completes the next Smalltalk-idiom step for the interactive workspace. The next clean work is command-model polish around `do it`, `print it`, `accept`, and save/reopen so the framebuffer editor feels less like an MVP transport surface and more like a real in-image tool.

## 2026-03-09 - Bridge The Interactive Editor Back Into The Browser Flow
- Completed the next browser/editor integration step on both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). The interactive workspace now has a `Ctrl-O` path that restores the saved underlying method/package browser target and reuses the normal `Workspace reopen` rendering path instead of trapping the user in a separate editor loop.
- Kept the design clean by factoring the existing `Workspace reopen` primitive body into an internal `workspace_reopen_in_place` helper. That means editor-to-browser return and ordinary reopen now share the exact same browser rendering logic, which avoids a second partial browser implementation growing inside the input monitor.
- Preserved the image-visible source buffer when returning to the browser. If you enter the editor from a method browser, the current buffer remains the workspace’s current source, so reopening the browser shows the live edited source buffer in that browser context even before `acceptCurrent`. That matches the Smalltalk-shaped “browser plus source buffer” model better than treating the editor as a detached text area.
- Added [examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_browser_bridge_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_browser_bridge_demo.rz) and strengthened [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py) with a focused RV32 proof. The new test boots into `Display>>newline`, enters the interactive editor, sends `Ctrl-O`, and proves the method browser is rendered again by observing the browser labels a second time.
- This completes the current browser/editor integration milestone for the interactive workspace track. The next clean milestone is snapshot/reopen of the live editor session so buffer contents, cursor position, viewport, and browser-linked editor context survive save/reload cleanly.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_return_to_its_browser_context tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_evaluate_current_buffer tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_accept_current_buffer -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Keep Interactive Run Feedback Visible In The Editor
- Added a small interactive-workspace status/output pane on both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). The input monitor now reserves a few lines at the bottom of the framebuffer editor for `STATUS` plus recent `OUT>` lines, instead of letting every `Ctrl-R` redraw erase the interesting result immediately.
- Kept the implementation minimal and inspectable by capturing writes only at the default-form text path while the interactive monitor is actively evaluating. `form_write_string` and `form_newline` append to a bounded feedback buffer only during that narrow window, so normal browser/editor rendering does not recursively capture itself and the VM does not need a second transcript subsystem just for the workspace.
- Wired the feedback pane into the existing editor commands. `Ctrl-R` now clears prior feedback, captures do-it output, and reports `RUN OK`; `Ctrl-X` reports install status and surfaces missing-browser cases as `ACCEPT NEEDS BROWSER` instead of silently doing nothing. This keeps the interactive workspace closer to a real in-image tool loop rather than a raw input shell.
- Strengthened the focused RV32 proof in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The interactive evaluate test now proves the editor redraw includes `STATUS: RUN OK` and an `OUT> 3` line after running `Transcript show: (1 + 2) printString.` from the workspace buffer.
- This completes the “better run feedback” milestone for the interactive workspace track. The next clean milestone is browser/editor integration so the framebuffer editor becomes the front end for the existing method/package browser flow instead of an adjacent tool surface.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_evaluate_current_buffer tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_accept_current_buffer -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Accept Browser Source Directly From The Interactive Workspace
- Extended the interactive workspace state on both runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) so the input monitor no longer throws away the underlying browser context. The serialized editor state now carries cursor position, viewport top line, and the saved browser view/target it came from. That keeps the editor small and inspectable without widening the `Workspace` object model just to remember one more layer of tool state.
- Added a dedicated editor-side install command on the primary RV32 path and mirrored it on RV64: `Ctrl-X` now restores the saved method/package browser target, runs the existing `Workspace acceptCurrent` logic, and then returns cleanly to the editor buffer. The method/package install path itself was factored into a shared helper so the editor uses the same source-owned install semantics as the browser surface instead of inventing a parallel host-ish shortcut.
- Kept the design aligned with the Smalltalk-shaped architecture: the interactive workspace remains a thin front end over the existing image-visible browser/compiler tools. The editor is not a separate subsystem with its own installer; it just preserves enough browser context to reuse the same image-owned accept path from the framebuffer window.

## 2026-03-09 - Make Interactive Source Readable On The Framebuffer
- Replaced the earlier placeholder uppercase-only text table on both QEMU runtimes with a broader 5x7 ASCII font in [platform/shared/font5x7.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/shared/font5x7.h), then switched [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) to include that shared table instead of carrying tiny divergent local glyph stubs. The font covers the practical Smalltalk/Recorz editing subset: lowercase, digits, and the source punctuation the interactive workspace needs (`:`, `|`, `^`, `[`, `]`, `<`, `>`, `+`, `-`, `*`, `/`, and friends).
- Kept the change aligned with the current architecture: this is still just seeded text behavior on the existing display/form/glyph path, not a new UI subsystem. The interactive workspace did not need new rendering logic; it simply became legible because the underlying glyph surface is now real instead of mostly placeholder boxes.
- Added [examples/qemu_riscv_source_glyph_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_source_glyph_demo.rz) and broadened [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_render_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_render_integration.py) with a focused framebuffer proof. The new test boots an RV32 image that draws lowercase selectors, digits, block brackets, temps bars, return carets, and common operators, then verifies the screenshot region contains real foreground glyph pixels rather than only background-filled character cells.
- Updated [platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile) so shared platform headers are explicit build dependencies. That keeps the new shared font surface honest for incremental rebuilds instead of relying on clean builds to notice it.
- This completes the “readable source on screen” milestone for the interactive workspace track. The next clean step is editor-side `accept`: let the existing input monitor install a method or package directly from the QEMU window without dropping back to host-side file-in.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector tests.test_qemu_riscv32_render_integration -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Correct Virtio Keyboard Letter Mapping For The Interactive Workspace
- Fixed the machine-layer virtio keyboard translation on both QEMU targets in [platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c). The initial window-input path treated letter key codes as one contiguous `A..Z` range, which is not true for the Linux/virtio key codes QEMU delivers. That made home-row keys drift alphabetically, so `D` rendered as `C`.
- Replaced that arithmetic shortcut with an explicit key-to-letter mapping helper and reused the same helper for control-key generation. This keeps the machine layer honest about the input code set instead of baking a PC-keyboard-layout accident into the editor path, and it avoids carrying a latent bug into the future hardware targets.
- Strengthened the focused RV32 keyboard integration proof in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The graphical QEMU test now injects `A`, `S`, `D`, and `F` through the QEMU monitor and proves that the live workspace buffer renders `ASDF`, which catches the earlier contiguous-range bug instead of only proving the single `A` case.
- This is a small but important cleanup step for the interactive workspace track: the QEMU-window input path is now trustworthy enough to keep building the editor on top of it, rather than forcing the human-facing UI back through the terminal serial fallback.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_accepts_virtio_keyboard_input -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Let The QEMU Window Feed The Interactive Workspace
- Extended the machine layer on the primary RV32 target in [platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c) so `machine_try_getc` and `machine_wait_getc` now consume input from either the existing UART path or a discovered virtio keyboard device. The workspace/editor code remains unchanged and still reads a byte stream, which keeps the interactive tools image-shaped instead of growing a separate UI-specific input subsystem.
- Reused the existing DTB discovery seam rather than hardcoding keyboard transport addresses. The `virt` machine already exposes `virtio,mmio` transports in the device tree, so the runtime now records those candidates alongside UART and `fw_cfg`, then binds the first virtio input device it finds during `machine_init`.
- Corrected the keyboard driver to match the QEMU transport the repo actually runs on today. Local QEMU exposes legacy virtio-mmio (`version = 1`) for `virtio-keyboard-device`, so the machine layer now initializes the legacy split-queue layout with a page-aligned queue region while still preserving the modern-path structure for later transport cleanup. This keeps the current RV32-first QEMU development path honest instead of assuming a newer transport contract than the platform provides.
- Added the user-facing hookup in [platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile) and mirrored the run-path parity on [platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/Makefile). `make ... run` and `make ... run-interactive` on RV32 now launch QEMU with `virtio-keyboard-device`, so the framebuffer window itself can feed the interactive workspace instead of relying only on terminal-backed serial input.
- Mirrored the same machine-layer discovery and virtio keyboard logic on the RV64 validation runtime in [platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c), keeping the secondary target aligned with the RV32-first interactive workspace path.
- Added a focused RV32 integration proof in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The new test boots the input monitor with a graphical QEMU instance, injects `shift-a` through the QEMU monitor, and proves that the workspace view advances to column 2 with `A` rendered in the live buffer. That is the first automated proof that the QEMU window input path reaches the running image rather than only the terminal serial path.
- This completes the next clean interactive-workspace milestone: the editor can now be driven from the QEMU window on the RV32 path. The main remaining usability gap is framebuffer glyph coverage for normal source text, especially lowercase and punctuation-heavy code, which is better handled as a separate rendering/data step than mixed into the keyboard transport work.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_accepts_virtio_keyboard_input tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_evaluate_current_buffer -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Let The Interactive Workspace Run The Current Editor Buffer
- Extended the interactive workspace editor on the primary RV32 VM in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) with an editor-local run command: `Ctrl-R` now evaluates the current input-monitor buffer as a workspace do-it without replacing the raw editor text with a normalized `RecorzKernelDoIt:` chunk. That is the smallest coherent move toward a real Smalltalk-style workspace: the buffer you are editing remains the buffer you see, while the runtime still remembers an executable do-it chunk for `rerun`.
- Kept the design image-aligned rather than host-driven. The new helper snapshots the current input-monitor view metadata, normalizes only the executable copy of the buffer, runs it through the existing workspace evaluator, then restores the input-monitor view, cursor state, and raw source binding. This preserves the current `Workspace`-owned editor session instead of introducing a second hidden evaluation surface.
- Updated the input monitor header on both QEMU runtimes in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c) to advertise the new `RUN: CTRL-R` command, and mirrored the same run-path logic on RV64 so the secondary validation target stays aligned with the RV32-first development path.
- Added a dedicated proof program in [examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_evaluate_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_evaluate_demo.rz) and extended [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The new serial integration test types a do-it into the live input monitor, runs it with `Ctrl-R`, continues editing, exits, and then proves that `Workspace rerun` re-executes the normalized last source while the visible editor buffer still contains the raw post-run text.
- This completes the first runnable editor step for the interactive workspace track. The framebuffer editor can now capture, edit, and execute the current buffer in place, but it still lacks in-editor accept/package install commands and a richer output pane. Those belong to the next steps rather than being hidden inside this milestone.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_supports_cursor_editing tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_supports_vertical_cursor_movement tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_scrolls_multiline_buffers tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_can_evaluate_current_buffer -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Add Vertical Navigation And Viewport Scrolling To The Interactive Workspace
- Extended the interactive workspace editor state on the primary RV32 VM in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) from a single cursor index into a small structured state record: cursor position plus top visible line. That keeps the editor state inside the existing `Workspace` object surface, so the image remains inspectable and snapshot-friendly without widening the MVP object layout.
- Added real vertical cursor motion to the serial-backed editor: up/down arrow keys and `Ctrl-P` / `Ctrl-N` now move between logical lines while preserving the current column where possible and clamping on short lines. Home/end behavior still works, and the existing horizontal editing path remains unchanged.
- Added viewport normalization and scrolling to the framebuffer input monitor view. The editor now tracks the top visible line, scrolls automatically as the cursor moves beyond the visible window, and renders the current `TOP`, `LINE`, and `COL` state in the workspace header. This is the first time the input monitor behaves like a true multiline workspace editor instead of a fixed top-of-buffer view.
- Mirrored the same cursor-state, vertical-motion, and viewport logic on the RV64 validation runtime in [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c), keeping the secondary target aligned with the RV32-first development path.
- Strengthened the RV32 serial integration coverage in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The new proofs cover horizontal cursor editing with the expanded movement legend, multiline vertical editing with `Ctrl-P` / `Ctrl-N`, and automatic top-line scrolling on a buffer large enough to exceed the visible workspace rows.
- This completes the basic navigation/editing milestone for the first interactive workspace slice. The editor still needs richer visible source text, scrolling commands beyond automatic cursor-following, and evaluate/accept key bindings, but it now has the minimum coherent multiline navigation behavior expected of a Smalltalk-shaped workspace.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_supports_cursor_editing tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_supports_vertical_cursor_movement tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_scrolls_multiline_buffers -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Add Cursor Editing To The RV32 Interactive Workspace Buffer
- Extended the interactive workspace input monitor in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) so it now has real editor-state instead of append-only capture. The buffer still lives in the image-visible `Workspace currentSource` slot, but cursor position is now preserved through the existing `currentTargetName` slot when the active view is `INPUT_MONITOR`. That is the smallest coherent move that stays faithful to the docs: editor state remains inspectable and snapshot-safe without widening the MVP object layout yet.
- Kept the editor-state encoding deliberately simple and RV32-friendly. The runtime now binds two stable static buffers into the workspace object while the interactive editor is active: one for the mutable source text and one for the encoded cursor state. This avoids leaking the finite runtime string pool on every keystroke while still allowing snapshots and regenerated source restore to carry the current buffer and cursor state forward.
- Broadened the RV32 input loop in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) from raw character append/backspace into true insertion editing with cursor motion. `Ctrl-B` / `Ctrl-F` and terminal left/right arrows move the cursor, `Ctrl-A` / `Ctrl-E` and Home/End jump to line start/end, insertion happens at the cursor, and backspace deletes before the cursor. This is still intentionally a tiny editor, but it crosses the important Phase-1 threshold from “serial capture” to “editable workspace buffer”.
- Added a tiny framebuffer-only cursor rendering primitive in [platform/qemu-riscv32/display.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/display.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/display.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/display.c), exposed through the matching headers. The workspace input view now shows move/home hints plus line/column state, and it paints a live cursor bar into the existing form surface instead of inventing a separate UI layer. That keeps the implementation aligned with the Smalltalk-shaped display/form path already in the image.
- Mirrored the same runtime/display contract on the RV64 validation path in [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c), [platform/qemu-riscv64/display.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/display.c), and [platform/qemu-riscv64/display.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/display.h), and cleaned up regenerated boot-source view restore on both QEMU targets so the input-monitor browser remains restorable even when no class/package target name is present.
- Strengthened the focused RV32 serial proof in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The test now drives the live editor with `ab`, `Ctrl-B`, `C`, `Ctrl-F`, `D`, and `Ctrl-D`, proving that the resulting workspace buffer is `aCbD` rather than append-only text. This is the first real editable-buffer proof for the interactive workspace track.
- This is the next clean milestone-2 step rather than the whole editor milestone. The system now has a cursor-aware editable text buffer on the existing framebuffer/serial workspace path, but it still lacks vertical navigation, scrolling, and evaluate/accept key bindings. That keeps the implementation small and clean while moving directly toward a usable in-image workspace.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_supports_cursor_editing -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`.

## 2026-03-09 - Add The First RV32 Interactive Workspace Input Path
- Extended the thin machine interface on both QEMU targets in [platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.c), [platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/machine.h), [platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.c), and [platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.h](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/machine.h) with non-blocking and blocking UART receive helpers. This is the smallest clean move that matches the docs: input enters through a machine/display bootstrap seam, not through host-only scripting or a separate editor framework.
- Added two deliberately narrow `Workspace` selectors in [kernel/mvp/Workspace.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Workspace.rz) and [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz): `browseInteractiveInput` and `interactiveInputMonitor`. The first gives the image a real browser/view state for the new surface; the second enters a modal serial-backed capture loop. This keeps the feature Smalltalk-shaped and inspectable, with `Workspace` remaining the tool model object rather than inventing a parallel hidden subsystem.
- Implemented the primary RV32 runtime path in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) and mirrored the same contract on the RV64 validation runtime in [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c). The new view renders the current source buffer raw instead of the older uppercase browser normalization, binds a dedicated mutable workspace editor buffer directly into `Workspace currentSource`, and updates that buffer from UART input with printable characters, backspace, newline, and `Ctrl-D` exit. That is intentionally only the first interactive slice: no cursor model, no selection model, and no broader UI framework yet.
- Kept the build/runtime envelope aligned by raising the selector ceilings in [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), and by extending the pinned lowering/binding expectations in [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py). This preserves the shared source-to-image contract instead of letting the new editor hook become an RV32-only ad hoc extension.
- Added the focused proof in [examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_demo.rz) and a new RV32 serial integration test in [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py). The live proof waits for the monitor view to appear, feeds `ab`, backspace, `C`, and `Ctrl-D` over QEMU serial, and proves that `Workspace contents` comes back as `aC`. I also added [platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/Makefile) target `run-interactive` so this feature has a clean manual entry point without QEMU monitor multiplexing on stdin.
- This completes milestone 1 for the interactive workspace track in the smallest coherent way. The system now has a real input path from QEMU into the live image and a framebuffer-backed workspace view that can hold typed source. It does not yet provide a full editor, cursor movement, or accept/evaluate key bindings, but it reaches the architectural threshold the docs call for: display/input bootstrap is now inside the same live, inspectable system as the workspace/browser tools.
- Verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering tests.test_qemu_riscv_image_inspector -v`, `python3 -m unittest tests.test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.QemuRiscv32SerialIntegrationTests.test_workspace_interactive_input_monitor_supports_cursor_editing -v`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 clean all inspect-image`, `make -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64 clean all inspect-image`, and `make -n -C /Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32 EXAMPLE=/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_input_monitor_demo.rz run-interactive`.

## 2026-03-09 - Make Regenerated Source Browsable In-Image Without Clobbering Snapshot State
- Extended the image-side `Workspace` surface in [kernel/mvp/Workspace.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Workspace.rz) and [kernel/mvp/Selector.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/kernel/mvp/Selector.rz) with `browseRegeneratedBootSource`, `browseRegeneratedKernelSource`, and a small bootstrap-only `seedBootContents:` hook. The first two move regeneration inspection onto the normal image/browser surface, while `seedBootContents:` preserves the earlier cold-boot “show me the current `.rz` source in the workspace” behavior without overloading ordinary user editing semantics.
- Reworked the primary RV32 runtime in [platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/vm.c) so regenerated boot/kernel source can be produced through the same emitter logic into an in-memory browser buffer as well as out over serial. The new regenerated-source workspace views are recomputed on demand instead of being persisted as giant ordinary workspace strings, which keeps snapshot/reopen behavior safe on the current RV32 MVP limits while still making the regenerated artifacts inspectable through `Workspace contents` and the framebuffer browser.
- Mirrored the same selector/view/runtime contract on the RV64 validation path in [platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/vm.c), plus the top-level selector ceilings in [platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv32/program.c) and [platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c](/Users/david/repos/recorz/platform/qemu-riscv64/program.c), so the shared seed/runtime envelope stays aligned while RV32 remains the primary development target.
- Moved the host-lowered top-level source-buffer prelude in [tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tools/build_qemu_riscv_mvp_image.py) from ordinary `setContents:` to the new `seedBootContents:` path, and taught both runtimes to ignore that bootstrap-only seed when resuming from a snapshot. This fixes an important self-hosting regression boundary: snapshot-owned workspace class/package source buffers now survive reload, so `Workspace fileInCurrent` after reboot uses the saved filed-out source instead of the reload demo’s host-side `.rz` source.
- Added focused proofs in [examples/qemu_riscv_in_image_regenerated_kernel_source_browser_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_in_image_regenerated_kernel_source_browser_demo.rz) and [examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_regenerated_boot_source_save_demo.rz](/Users/david/repos/recorz/examples/qemu_riscv_workspace_regenerated_boot_source_save_demo.rz), and extended coverage in [tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv_mvp_lowering.py), [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_serial_integration.py), [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_snapshot_integration.py), and [tests/test_qemu_riscv32_regeneration_integration.py](/Users/david/repos/recorz/tests/test_qemu_riscv32_regeneration_integration.py). The key RV32 proofs now cover browsing regenerated kernel source inside the image, reopening a regenerated boot-source browser from a saved snapshot, and preserving existing class/package file-out buffers across snapshot resume.
- This is the next clean self-hosting-path step rather than a detour: regeneration artifacts are now visible through normal image tools, and snapshot resume no longer lets the host-side launcher source overwrite saved in-image development state. That keeps the day-to-day development loop centered in the image while still leaving the host builder as packaging/validation infrastructure.
